     <p>In 2012–2013, Notre Dame ranked 17th overall among &quot;national universities&quot; in the United States in <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>'</i>s <i>Best Colleges 2013</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Forbes.com" title="Forbes.com" class="mw-redirect">Forbes.com</a>'s <i>America's Best Colleges</i> ranks Notre Dame 12th among colleges in the United States for 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> also lists Notre Dame Law School as 22nd overall.<sup id="cite_ref-NDLaw_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDLaw-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a></i> ranks Mendoza College of Business undergraduate school as 1st overall.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> It ranks the MBA program as 20th overall. Additionally, <i>The Washington Monthly</i> ranked the university 13th nationally in its 2006 edition.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_Gourmet_Report" title="Philosophical Gourmet Report">Philosophical Gourmet Report</a> ranks Notre Dame's graduate philosophy program as 15th nationally,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i>ARCHITECT</i> Magazine ranked the undergraduate architecture program as 12th nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The Princeton Review rated Notre Dame as the sixth most LGBT-Unfriendly College in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" title="Study abroad" class="mw-redirect">study abroad</a> program ranks sixth in highest participation percentage in the nation, with 57.6% of students choosing to study abroad in 17 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> According to payscale.com, undergraduate alumni of University of Notre Dame have a mid-career median salary $121,000, making it the 8th highest among colleges and universities in the United States. The median starting salary of $55,300 ranked 41st in the same peer group.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Named by <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> as one of the &quot;25 New <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivies</a>,&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> it is also an <a href="/wiki/Oak_Ridge_Associated_Universities" title="Oak Ridge Associated Universities">Oak Ridge Associated University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zahm">Zahm</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Zahm">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Father Joseph Carrier, C.S.C. was Director of the Science Museum and the Library and Professor of Chemistry and Physics until 1874. Carrier taught that scientific research and its promise for progress were not antagonistic to the ideals of intellectual and moral culture endorsed by the Church. One of Carrier's students was Father <a href="/wiki/John_Zahm" title="John Zahm" class="mw-redirect">John Zahm</a> (1851–1921) who was made Professor and Co-Director of the Science Department at age 23 and by 1900 was a nationally prominent scientist and naturalist. Zahm was active in the Catholic Summer School movement, which introduced Catholic laity to contemporary intellectual issues. His book <i>Evolution and Dogma</i> (1896) defended certain aspects of evolutionary theory as true, and argued, moreover, that even the great Church teachers Thomas Aquinas and Augustine taught something like it. The intervention of Irish American Catholics in Rome prevented Zahm's censure by the Vatican. In 1913, Zahm and former President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> embarked on a major expedition through the Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_science">Other science</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other science">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1882, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Francis_Zahm" title="Albert Francis Zahm">Albert Zahm</a> (John Zahm's brother) built an early <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnel</a> used to compare lift to drag of aeronautical models. Around 1899, Professor Jerome Green became the first American to send a wireless message. In 1931, Father <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nieuwland" title="Julius Nieuwland">Julius Nieuwland</a> performed early work on basic reactions that was used to create <a href="/wiki/Neoprene" title="Neoprene">neoprene</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Study of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a> at the university began with the building of a <a href="/wiki/Particle_accelerator" title="Particle accelerator">nuclear accelerator</a> in 1936,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and continues now partly through a partnership in the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Institute_for_Nuclear_Astrophysics" title="Joint Institute for Nuclear Astrophysics">Joint Institute for Nuclear Astrophysics</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lobund_Institute">Lobund Institute</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lobund Institute">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Lobund Institute grew out of pioneering research in germ-free-life which began in 1928. This area of research originated in a question posed by Pasteur as to whether animal life was possible without bacteria. Though others had taken up this idea, their research was short lived and inconclusive. Lobund was the first research organization to answer definitively, that such life is possible and that it can be prolonged through generations. But the objective was not merely to answer Pasteur's question but also to produce the germ free animal as a new tool for biological and medical research. This objective was reached and for years Lobund was a unique center for the study and production of germ free animals and for their use in biological and medical investigations. Today the work has spread to other universities. In the beginning it was under the Department of Biology and a program leading to the master's degree accompanied the research program. In the 1940s Lobund achieved independent status as a purely research organization and in 1950 was raised to the status of an Institute. In 1958 it was brought back into the Department of Biology as integral part of that department, but with its own program leading to the degree of PhD in Gnotobiotics.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG/170px-University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG/255px-University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG/340px-University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Notre_Dame_Hallway.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hallway within Hurley Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: English">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Richard_T._Sullivan" title="Richard T. Sullivan">Richard T. Sullivan</a> taught English from 1936 to 1974 and published six novels, dozens of short stories, and various other efforts. He was known as a regional writer and a Catholic spokesman.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Frank O'Malley was an English professor during the 1930s–1960s. Influenced by Jacques Maritain, John U. Nef, and others, O'Malley developed a concept of Christian philosophy that was a fundamental element in his thought. Through his course &quot;Modern Catholic Writers&quot; O'Malley introduced generations of undergraduates to Gabriel Marcel, Graham Greene, Evelyn Waugh, Sigrid Undset, Paul Claudel, and Gerard Manley Hopkins.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_.C3.A9migr.C3.A9s">European &eacute;migr&eacute;s</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: European &eacute;migr&eacute;s">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The rise of Hitler and other dictators in the 1930s forced numerous Catholic intellectuals to flee Europe; president <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_O%27Hara" title="John Francis O'Hara">John O’Hara</a> brought many to Notre Dame. From Germany came Anton-Hermann Chroust (1907–1982) in classics and law,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> and Waldemar Gurian a German Catholic intellectual of Jewish descent. Positivism dominated American intellectual life in the 1920s onward but in marked contrast, Gurian received a German Catholic education and wrote his doctoral dissertation under Max Scheler.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Me%C5%A1trovi%C4%87" title="Ivan Meštrović">Ivan Meštrović</a> (1883–1962), a renowned sculptor, brought Croatian culture to campus, 1955–62.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yves_Simon" title="Yves Simon">Yves Simon</a> (1903–61), brought to ND in the 1940s the insights of French studies in the Aristotelian-Thomistic tradition of philosophy; his own teacher <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Maritain" title="Jacques Maritain">Jacques Maritain</a> (1882–73) was a frequent visitor to campus.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The exiles developed a distinctive emphasis on the evils of totalitarianism. For example the political science courses of Gerhart Niemeyer (1907–97) discussed communist ideology and were particularly accessible to his students. He came to ND in 1955, and was a frequent contributor to the <i>National Review</i> and other conservative magazines.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_science">Political science</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Political science">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><i>The Review of Politics</i> was founded in 1939 by Gurian, modeled after German Catholic journals. It quickly emerged as part of an international Catholic intellectual revival, offering an alternative vision to positivist philosophy. For 44 years, the <i>Review</i> was edited by Gurian, Matthew Fitzsimons, Frederick Crosson, and Thomas Stritch. Intellectual leaders included Gurian, Jacques Maritain, Frank O'Malley, Leo Richard Ward, F. A. Hermens, and John U. Nef. It became a major forum for political ideas and modern political concerns, especially from a Catholic and scholastic tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_2">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> research continued in many fields. The university president, John Jenkins, described his hope that Notre Dame would become &quot;one of the pre–eminent research institutions in the world&quot; in his inaugural address.<sup id="cite_ref-Jenkins_address_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jenkins_address-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has many multi-disciplinary institutes devoted to research in varying fields, including the Medieval Institute, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kellogg_Institute_for_International_Studies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kellogg Institute for International Studies (page does not exist)">Kellogg Institute for International Studies</a>, the Kroc Institute for International <a href="/wiki/Peace_and_conflict_studies" title="Peace and conflict studies">Peace studies</a>, and the Center for Social Concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Recent research includes work on family conflict and child development,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Genome_project" title="Genome project">genome mapping</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> the increasing <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">trade deficit</a> of the United States with China,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> studies in <a href="/wiki/Fluid_mechanics" title="Fluid mechanics">fluid mechanics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> and marketing trends on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Endowment">Endowment</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Endowment">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Notre Dame's <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">financial endowment</a> was started in the early 1920s by university president James Burns, and increased to US$7&nbsp;million by 1952 when Hesburgh became president. By the 1980s it reached $150&nbsp;million, and in 2000, it returned a record 57.9% investment.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> For the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a>, the endowment had grown to approximately $6.5&nbsp;billion, putting the university in the top-15 largest endowments in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Endowment_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Endowment-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2012, Notre Dame's endowment is valued at $6.33&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Endowment_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Endowment-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>In 2009 the Notre Dame student body consisted of 11,733 students, with 8,371 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduates</a> and 3,362 <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate and professional</a> students.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_Profile_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_Profile-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Around 21–24% of students are children of <a href="/wiki/Alumnus" title="Alumnus">alumni</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> and although 37% of students come from the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a>, the student body represents all 50 states and 100 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_Profile_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_Profile-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> ranks the school as the fifth highest &quot;dream school&quot; for parents to send their children.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The school has been previously criticized for its lack of diversity,<sup id="cite_ref-Faith_at_ND_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faith_at_ND-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>The Princeton Review</i> ranks the university highly among schools at which &quot;Alternative Lifestyles [are] Not an Alternative.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> However, it has also been commended by some diversity oriented publications; <i>Hispanic Magazine</i> ranks the university ninth on its list of the top–25 colleges for <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Latinos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <i>Journal of Blacks in Higher Education</i> recognizes the university for raising enrollment of African-American students.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> With 6,000 participants, the university's <a href="/wiki/Intramural_sports" title="Intramural sports">intramural sports</a> program has been named by <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> as the best program in the country,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i>The Princeton Review</i> named it as the top school where &quot;Everyone Plays Intramural Sports.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The annual Bookstore Basketball tournament is the largest outdoor five-on-five tournament in the world with over 700 teams participating each year,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> while the Notre Dame Men's <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a> Club hosts the annual <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Bouts" title="Bengal Bouts">Bengal Bouts</a> tournament that raises money for the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_of_Holy_Cross#The_Mission_of_Holy_Cross_in_Bangladesh" title="Congregation of Holy Cross">Holy Cross Missions</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The strictly measured federal graduation rate for athletes was 86% for freshmen who entered between 2000 and 2002. This is one of the highest in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residence_halls">Residence halls</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Residence halls">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_residence_halls_at_the_University_of_Notre_Dame" title="List of residence halls at the University of Notre Dame">List of residence halls at the University of Notre Dame</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:South_Quad,_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/South_Quad%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/220px-South_Quad%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/South_Quad%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/330px-South_Quad%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/South_Quad%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/440px-South_Quad%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:South_Quad,_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view of South Quad, which houses a large number of undergraduates.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>About 80% of undergraduates and 20% of graduate students live on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_Profile_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_Profile-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The majority of the graduate students on campus live in one of four graduate housing complexes on campus, while all on-campus undergraduates live in one of the 29 residence halls.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of the religious affiliation of the university, all residence halls are single-sex, with 15 male dorms and 14 female dorms.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> The university maintains a visiting policy (known as parietal hours) for those students who live in dormitories, specifying times when members of the opposite sex are allowed to visit other students' dorm rooms; however, all residence halls have 24-hour social spaces for students regardless of gender. Many residence halls have at least one nun and/or priest as a resident. There are no traditional social <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities or sororities</a> at the university, but a majority of students live in the same residence hall for all four years. Some intramural sports are based on residence hall teams, where the university offers the only non-<a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">military academy</a> program of full-contact intramural American football.<sup id="cite_ref-Life_FAQ_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life_FAQ-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of the intramural season, the championship game is played on the field in <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Stadium" title="Notre Dame Stadium">Notre Dame Stadium</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_life">Religious life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Religious life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_of_Holy_Cross" title="Congregation of Holy Cross">Congregation of Holy Cross</a>. More than 93% of students identify as Christian, with over 80% of the total being Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> The Basilica of the Sacred Heart is on campus and each residence hall has a chapel. Collectively, <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Catholic Mass</a> is celebrated over 100 times per week on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-Life_FAQ_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life_FAQ-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> There are multitudes of religious statues and artwork around campus, most prominent of which are the statue of Mary on the Main Building, the Notre Dame Grotto, and the Word of Life mural on Hesburgh Library depicting Christ as a teacher. Additionally, every classroom displays a <a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">crucifix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Faith_at_ND_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faith_at_ND-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> There are many religious clubs at the school, including Council #1477 of the <a href="/wiki/Knights_of_Columbus" title="Knights of Columbus">Knights of Columbus</a> (KOC), <a href="/wiki/Baptist_Student_Union" title="Baptist Student Union">Baptist Collegiate Ministry (BCM)</a>, Jewish Club, Muslim Student Association, Orthodox Christian Fellowship, The Mormon Club, and many more. The Notre Dame KofC are known for being the first collegiate council of KofC, operating a charitable <a href="/wiki/Concession_stand" title="Concession stand">concession stand</a> during every home football game and owning their own building on campus which can be used as a cigar lounge.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG/220px-University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG/330px-University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG/440px-University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Notre_Dame_Golden_Dome.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Golden Dome of the Main Building with the Basilica of the Sacred Heart in the foreground.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University was founded by a group of Catholic missionary priests and brothers from France, members of the Congregation of Holy Cross (in Latin, Congregatio a Sancta Cruce; more commonly referred to as &quot;CSC,&quot; which is also the initials placed after all members' names). The land where they founded the school was donated to them by the Bishop of Vincennes, Indiana. They saw a large part of their early mission to be caring for and evangelizing the local <a href="/wiki/Potawatomi" title="Potawatomi">Potawatomi</a> tribes. Upon arrival on the lake shore in the cold of winter, they dedicated their new school and all their endeavors to the Virgin Mary under the name Notre Dame du Lac, which is French for Our Lady of the Lake.</p> 
     <p>This Catholic mission of the Congregation, its schools at the site, and their successors has shaped the campus and the university. Fifty-seven chapels are located throughout the campus.</p> 
     <p>While religious affiliation is not a criterion for admission, approximately 80% of undergraduates enrolled self-identify as Catholic. There are many Catholic clubs, organizations, and ministries on campus. There is a large campus ministry program and many volunteer opportunities. There is no compulsory participation in any religious liturgies. Students and clubs of other religions and Christian denominations are welcomed and supported.</p> 
     <p>Nearly every residence hall has a priest in residence. Every residence hall (and many academic buildings) contains a chapel, where Sunday and daily masses are celebrated during the school year. One dorm is named after a saint (Saint Edward). Sunday and daily masses as well as daily confessions are held in the Basilica of the Sacred Heart in the center of campus.</p> 
     <p>Architecturally, the school has a Catholic character. Atop the Main Building's gold dome is a golden statue of the Virgin Mary. Immediately in front of the Main Building and facing it, is a copper statue of Christ with arms upraised with the legend &quot;Venite Ad Me Omnes&quot; (&quot;Come to me, all you&quot;; Matthew 11:28a). Next to the Main Building is the Basilica of the Sacred Heart. Immediately behind the basilica is the Grotto, a Marian place of prayer and reflection. It is a replica of the grotto at <a href="/wiki/Lourdes" title="Lourdes">Lourdes</a>, France where Mary is reputed to have appeared to St. Bernadette in 1858. At the end of the main drive (and in a direct line that connects through 3 statues and the Gold Dome), is a simple, modern stone statue of Mary. Behind her approximately 1,000 feet (300&nbsp;m) is a statue of the founder of the school, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Sorin" title="Edward Sorin">Edward Sorin</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart,_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/170px-Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/255px-Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/340px-Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart%2C_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Basilica_of_the_Sacred_Heart,_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The interior of the Basilica of the Sacred Heart.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The 14-story Hesburgh Library sports a 134-foot-tall (41&nbsp;m) stone mosaic on its southern face of Christ surrounded by the Apostles and notable scholarly saints and doctors of the Church. This mosaic is entitled &quot;The Word of Life,&quot; but is affectionately referred to as 'Touchdown Jesus' because of Christ's upraised arms and the visibility of the mosaic from the stadium through the uprights of the northern endzone. Next to the library is <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Me%C5%A1trovi%C4%87" title="Ivan Meštrović">Ivan Meštrović</a>'s large bronze statue of Moses with finger upraised (affectionately known as 'Firstdown Moses').</p> 
     <p>The university is the major seat of the Congregation of Holy Cross (albeit not its official headquarters, which are in Rome). Its main seminary, Moreau Seminary, is located on the campus across St. Joseph lake from the Main Building. <a href="/wiki/Old_College,_University_of_Notre_Dame" title="Old College, University of Notre Dame">Old College</a>, the oldest building on campus and located near the shore of St. Mary lake, houses undergraduate seminarians. Retired priests and brothers reside in Fatima House (a former retreat center), Holy Cross House, as well as Columba Hall near the Grotto. Until the 1970s, many of the support staff were nuns and monks.</p> 
     <p>The university supports many Church-related organizations and ministries.</p> 
     <p>The university has a highly regarded theology program, both undergraduate and graduate, with many scholars, including Lawrence Cunningham, John Cavadini, and Gary Anderson. The chair of the department, John Cavadini, was appointed to the <a href="/wiki/International_Theological_Commission" title="International Theological Commission">International Theological Commission</a> by Pope Benedict XVI in 2010; Prof. Brian Daley, SJ, received the <a href="/wiki/Ratzinger_Foundation#Ratzinger_Prize" title="Ratzinger Foundation">Ratzinger Prize</a> in Theology in 2012.</p> 
     <p>University by-laws require that the President of the University be a priest of the United States Province of the Congregation of Holy Cross. Until 1967, when governance was transferred to a lay board of trustees, the university was entirely governed by the leadership of the Holy Cross order.</p> 
     <p>Although the faculty was well over 85% Catholic before 1970, search practices have broadened. In recent years about half the new faculty hires have been Catholics, and Catholics now comprise 52% of the faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>However, in a policy statement the University declares that &quot;the Catholic identity of the University depends upon ... the continuing presence of a predominant number of Catholic intellectuals&quot; on the faculty. As the provost has explained, the aim is &quot;to have a majority of faculty who are Catholic, who understand the nature of the religion, who can be living role models, who can talk with students about issues outside the classroom and can infuse values into what they do.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/220px-Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/330px-Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG/440px-Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Grotto_University_of_Notre_Dame.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Grotto to 
        <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Our Lady of Lourdes">Our Lady of Lourdes</a>, one of the many spiritual places on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2009 the University was criticized by many Catholic bishops for conferring an honorary degree on President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>. President Obama's promotion of abortion access and types of <a href="/wiki/Embryonic_stem_cell" title="Embryonic stem cell">embryonic stem cell</a> research that result in the destruction of human embryos conflicts with Catholic doctrine on the <a href="/wiki/Sanctity_of_life" title="Sanctity of life">sanctity of life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student-run_media">Student-run media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Student-run media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As at most other universities, Notre Dame's students run a number of news media outlets. The nine student-run outlets include three newspapers, both a radio and television station, and several magazines and journals. The newspapers have varying publication interests, with <i>The Observer</i> published daily and mainly reporting university and other news.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Observer</i> is staffed by students from both Notre Dame and Saint Mary's College, the women's college located nearby. Unlike <i>Scholastic</i> and <i>The Dome,</i> <i>The Observer</i> is an independent publication and does not have a faculty advisor or any editorial oversight from the University. In 1987, when some students believed that <i>The Observer</i> began to show a conservative bias, a liberal newspaper, <i>Common Sense</i> was published. Likewise, in 2003, when other students believed that the paper showed a liberal bias, the conservative paper <i>Irish Rover</i> went into production. Neither paper is published as often as <i>The Observer</i>; however, all three are distributed to all students.<sup id="cite_ref-Publications_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Publications-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The television station, NDtv, grew from one show in 2002 to a full 24-hour channel with original programming by September 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WSND-FM" title="WSND-FM">WSND-FM</a> serves the student body and larger South Bend community at 88.9 FM, offering students a chance to become involved in bringing classical music, fine arts and educational programming, and alternative rock to the airwaves. Another radio station, WVFI, began as a partner of WSND-FM. More recently, however, WVFI has been airing independently and is streamed on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Begun as a one-page journal in September 1876,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/Scholastic_(Notre_Dame_publication)" title="Scholastic (Notre Dame publication)">Scholastic</a></i> magazine is issued twice monthly and claims to be the oldest continuous collegiate publication in the United States. The other magazine, <i>The Juggler</i>, is released twice a year and focuses on student literature and artwork.<sup id="cite_ref-Publications_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Publications-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Dome</i> yearbook is published annually. Finally, in Spring 2008 an undergraduate journal for political science research, <i>Beyond Politics</i>, made its debut.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_development">Community development</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Community development">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" /></a></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">This section requires <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit">expansion</a>. <small><i>(November 2012)</i></small></span></td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The first phase of Eddy Street Commons, a $215&nbsp;million development located adjacent to the University of Notre Dame campus and funded by the university, broke ground on June 3, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The Eddy Street Commons drew union protests when workers hired by the City of South Bend to construct the public parking garage picketed the private work site after a contractor hired non-union workers.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The developer, Kite Realty out of Indianapolis, has made agreements with major national chains rather than local businesses, a move that has led to criticism from alumni and students.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish">Notre Dame Fighting Irish</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Notre Dame teams are known as the Fighting Irish. They compete as a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> level (non-football sub-level), primarily competing in the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">Big East Conference</a> for all sports since the 1995-96 season.<sup id="cite_ref-Athletics_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Athletics-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> The Fighting Irish previously competed in the <a href="/wiki/Horizon_League" title="Horizon League">Horizon League</a> from 1982-83 to 1985-86, and again from 1987-88 to 1994-95. Men's sports include baseball, basketball, crew, cross country, fencing, football, golf, ice hockey, lacrosse, soccer, swimming &amp; diving, tennis and track &amp; field; while women's sports include basketball, cross country, fencing, golf, lacrosse, rowing, soccer, softball, swimming &amp; diving, tennis, track &amp; field and volleyball. The football team competes as an Football Bowl Subdivision (FBS) <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_independent_schools" title="NCAA Division I FBS independent schools">Independent</a><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> since its inception in 1887. Both <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">fencing</a> teams compete in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Midwest_Fencing_Conference&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Midwest Fencing Conference (page does not exist)">Midwest Fencing Conference</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> and the men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team competes in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Central Collegiate Hockey Association">Central Collegiate Hockey Association</a> (CCHA).<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In July 2013, Notre Dame will have new conference homes for all of its sports except football and fencing as a result of <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_NCAA_conference_realignment" title="2010–13 NCAA conference realignment">major conference realignment</a>. The Irish will leave the Big East for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC);<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> while they will maintain their football independence, they have committed to play five games per season against ACC opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> In ice hockey, the Irish were forced to find a new conference home after the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>'s decision to add the sport in 2013–14 led to <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9313_NCAA_conference_realignment#Hockey" title="2010–13 NCAA conference realignment">a cascade of conference moves</a> that culminated in the dissolution of the CCHA after the 2012–13 season. Notre Dame will move its hockey team to <a href="/wiki/Hockey_East" title="Hockey East">Hockey East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Fighting Irish name was used in the early 1920s with respect to the football team and was popularized by alumnus Francis Wallace in his <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i> columns.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> The official colors of Notre Dame are gold and blue<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> which are worn in competition by its athletic teams. In addition, the color green is often worn because of the Fighting Irish nickname.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Leprechaun" title="Notre Dame Leprechaun">Notre Dame Leprechaun</a> is the mascot of the athletic teams. Created by <a href="/wiki/Theodore_W._Drake" title="Theodore W. Drake">Theodore W. Drake</a> in 1964, the leprechaun was first used on the football pocket schedule and later on the football program covers. The leprechaun was featured on the cover of <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i></a> in November 1964 and gained national exposure.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In September 2012, however, Notre Dame announced that it would leave the Big East and join the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC) for all sports except football and men's hockey, with the exact date of the conference move to be determined.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> The university <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a> plays at home games for most of the sports. The band, which began in 1846 and has a claim as the oldest university band in continuous existence in the United States, was honored by the National Music Council as a &quot;Landmark of American Music&quot; during the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bicentennial" title="United States Bicentennial">United States Bicentennial</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> The band regularly plays the school's <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> the <i><a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Victory_March" title="Notre Dame Victory March" class="mw-redirect">Notre Dame Victory March</a></i>, which was named as the most played and most famous fight song by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Illinois_University" title="Northern Illinois University">Northern Illinois</a> Professor <a href="/wiki/William_Studwell" title="William Studwell">William Studwell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-leroux_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leroux-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i>College Fight Songs: An Annotated Anthology</i> published in 1998, the &quot;Notre Dame Victory March&quot; ranks as the greatest fight song of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-leroux_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leroux-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to some analysts without direct connection to the university or its athletic department, Notre Dame promotes <a href="/wiki/Muscular_Christianity" title="Muscular Christianity">Muscular Christianity</a> through its athletic programs.<sup id="cite_ref-C.26P_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26P-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sponsors_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sponsors-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Neither the university nor its athletic department have ever commented on this assertion.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame Fighting Irish football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Notre-dame-stadium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Notre-dame-stadium.jpg/220px-Notre-dame-stadium.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Notre-dame-stadium.jpg/330px-Notre-dame-stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Notre-dame-stadium.jpg/440px-Notre-dame-stadium.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Notre-dame-stadium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Stadium" title="Notre Dame Stadium">Notre Dame Stadium</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Notre Dame football team has a long history, first beginning when the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines_football" title="Michigan Wolverines football">Michigan Wolverines football</a> team brought football to Notre Dame in 1887 and played against a group of students.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> In the long history since then, 13 Fighting Irish teams have won consensus <a href="/wiki/College_football_national_championships_in_NCAA_Division_I_FBS" title="College football national championships in NCAA Division I FBS">national championships</a> (although the university only claims 11),<sup id="cite_ref-Athletics_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Athletics-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> along with another nine teams being named national champion by at least one source.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the program has the most members in the <a href="/wiki/College_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="College Football Hall of Fame">College Football Hall of Fame</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> is tied with <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_football" title="Ohio State Buckeyes football">Ohio State University</a> with the most <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophies</a> won,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> and have the second highest <a href="/wiki/Winning_percentage" title="Winning percentage">winning percentage</a> in NCAA history.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> With the long history, Notre Dame has accumulated many <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football_rivalries" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football rivalries">rivals</a>, and its annual game against <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_football" title="USC Trojans football">USC</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Jeweled_Shillelagh" title="Jeweled Shillelagh">Jeweled Shillelagh</a> has been named by some as one of the most important in college football<sup id="cite_ref-greatest_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greatest-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> and is often called the greatest intersectional rivalry in college football in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-USCNDtheGreatest_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCNDtheGreatest-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ESPN112406_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN112406-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SI101205_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SI101205-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT102007_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT102007-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PAC112006_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAC112006-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/George_Gipp" title="George Gipp">George Gipp</a> was the school’s legendary football player during 1916–20. He played semiprofessional baseball and smoked, drank, and gambled when not playing sports. He was also humble, generous to the needy, and a man of integrity.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> It was in 1928 that famed coach <a href="/wiki/Knute_Rockne" title="Knute Rockne">Knute Rockne</a> used his final conversation with the dying Gipp to inspire the Notre Dame team to beat the <a href="/wiki/Army_Black_Knights_football" title="Army Black Knights football">Army team</a> and &quot;win one for the Gipper.&quot; The 1940 film, <i><a href="/wiki/Knute_Rockne,_All_American" title="Knute Rockne, All American">Knute Rockne, All American</a></i>, starred <a href="/wiki/Pat_O%27Brien_(actor)" title="Pat O'Brien (actor)">Pat O'Brien</a> as Knute Rockne and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> as Gipp.</p> 
     <p>Today the team competes in <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Stadium" title="Notre Dame Stadium">Notre Dame Stadium</a>, an 80,795-seat stadium on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> The current head coach is <a href="/wiki/Brian_Kelly_(American_football_coach)" title="Brian Kelly (American football coach)">Brian Kelly</a>, hired from the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bearcats_football" title="Cincinnati Bearcats football">University of Cincinnati</a> on December 11, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> Kelly's record in three seasons at Notre Dame is 28–11.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> He succeeded <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Weis" title="Charlie Weis">Charlie Weis</a>, who was fired in November 2009 after five seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Weis led his team to two <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">Bowl Championship Series</a> <a href="/wiki/Bowl_game" title="Bowl game">bowl games</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> his overall record was 35–27,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> mediocre by Notre Dame standards, and the <a href="/wiki/2007_Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football_team" title="2007 Notre Dame Fighting Irish football team">2007 team</a> had the most losses in school history.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> The football team generates enough revenue to operate independently while $22.1&nbsp;million is retained from the team's profits for academic use. <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> named the team as the most valuable in college football, worth a total of $101&nbsp;million in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football_Gameday_Traditions">Football Gameday Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Football Gameday Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>During home games, activities occur all around campus and different dorms decorate their halls with a traditional item (e.g. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zahm_House&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zahm House (page does not exist)">Zahm House</a>'s two-story banner). Traditional activities begin at the stroke of midnight with the Drummers' Circle. This tradition involves the drum line of the <a href="/wiki/Band_of_the_Fighting_Irish" title="Band of the Fighting Irish">Band of the Fighting Irish</a> and ushers in the rest of the festivities that will continue the rest of the gameday Saturday. Later that day, the trumpet section will play the <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Victory_March" title="Notre Dame Victory March" class="mw-redirect">Notre Dame Victory March</a> and the Notre Dame Alma Mater under the dome. The band entire will play a concert at the steps of Bond Hall, from where they will march into <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Stadium" title="Notre Dame Stadium">Notre Dame Stadium</a>, leading fans and students alike across campus to the game.<sup id="cite_ref-ND_Gamedayl_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ND_Gamedayl-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Men's basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_men%27s_basketball" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's basketball">Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The men's basketball team has over 1,600 wins, one of only 12 schools who have reached that mark, and have appeared in 28 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA tournaments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBall_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBall-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> Former player <a href="/wiki/Austin_Carr" title="Austin Carr">Austin Carr</a> holds the record for most points scored in a single game of the tournament with 61.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> Although the team has never won the NCAA Tournament, they were named by the <a href="/wiki/Helms_Athletic_Foundation" title="Helms Athletic Foundation">Helms Athletic Foundation</a> as national champions twice.<sup id="cite_ref-BBall_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBall-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> The team has orchestrated a number of <a href="/wiki/Upset" title="Upset">upsets</a> of number one ranked teams, the most notable of which was ending <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins_men%27s_basketball" title="UCLA Bruins men's basketball">UCLA</a>'s record 88-game winning streak in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> The team has beaten an additional eight number-one teams, and those nine wins rank second, to UCLA's 10, all-time in wins against the top team.<sup id="cite_ref-BBall_203-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBall-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> The team plays in newly renovated Purcell Pavilion, which opened for the beginning of the 2009–2010 season,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> The team is coached by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Brey" title="Mike Brey">Mike Brey</a>, who, as of the 2011–12 season, his twelfth, has achieved a 259–130 record.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> Just in 2009 they were invited to the NIT, where they advanced to the semifinals but were beaten by Penn State who went on and beat Baylor in the championship. The 2010–11 team concluded its regular season ranked number seven in the country, with a record of 25–5, Brey's fifth straight 20-win season, and a second place finish in the Big East.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_women%27s_basketball" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish women's basketball">Notre Dame Fighting Irish women's basketball</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's ice hockey">Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's ice hockey</a>,&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's lacrosse">Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's lacrosse</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Notre Dame has been successful in other sports besides football, with an additional 14 national championships in various sports. Three teams have won multiple national championships with the fencing team leading them with seven,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> followed by the men's tennis and women's soccer teams each with two.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-past_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-past-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> The men's <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-past_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-past-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> men's golf,<sup id="cite_ref-past_210-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-past-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> and women's basketball teams have each won one in their histories.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the first ten years that Notre Dame competed in the Big East Conference its teams won a total of 64 championships.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006–07, Notre Dame's hockey team finished the regular season ranked #1.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The women's swimming and diving team holds the Big East record for consecutive conference championships in any sport with 14 straight conference titles (1997–2010).<span class="citation pressrelease"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.und.com/sports/w-swim/recaps/022010aaa.html">&quot;Notre Dame Claims 14th Consecutive BIG EAST Title&quot;</a> (Press release). University of Notre Dame Sports Information<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved May 17, 2010</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Notre+Dame&amp;rft.btitle=Notre+Dame+Claims+14th+Consecutive+BIG+EAST+Title&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.und.com%2Fsports%2Fw-swim%2Frecaps%2F022010aaa.html&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Notre+Dame+Sports+Information&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Band_of_the_Fighting_Irish" title="Band of the Fighting Irish">Band of the Fighting Irish</a> is the oldest university band in continuous existence.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> It was formed in 1846. The all-male Glee Club was formed in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The &quot;<a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Victory_March" title="Notre Dame Victory March" class="mw-redirect">Notre Dame Victory March</a>&quot; is the <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> for the University of Notre Dame. It was written by two brothers who were Notre Dame graduates. The Rev. Michael J. Shea, a 1904 graduate, wrote the music, and his brother, John F. Shea, who earned degrees in 1906 and 1908, wrote the original lyrics. The lyrics were revised in the 1920s; it first appeared under the copyright of the University of Notre Dame in 1928. The chorus is, &quot;Cheer cheer for old Notre Dame, wake up the echos cheering her name. Send a volley cheer on high, shake down the thunder from the sky! What though the odds be great or small, old Notre Dame will win over all. While her loyal sons are marching, onward to victory!&quot;</p> 
     <p>The chorus of the song is one of the most recognizable collegiate fight songs in the United States, and was ranked first among fight songs by Northern Illinois University Professor William Studwell, who remarked it was &quot;more borrowed, more famous and, frankly, you just hear it more.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-leroux_177-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leroux-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the film <i><a href="/wiki/Knute_Rockne,_All_American" title="Knute Rockne, All American">Knute Rockne, All American</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Knute_Rockne" title="Knute Rockne">Knute Rockne</a> (played by <a href="/wiki/Pat_O%27Brien_(actor)" title="Pat O'Brien (actor)">Pat O'Brien</a>) delivers the famous &quot;Win one for the Gipper&quot; speech, at which point the background music swells with the <i>Notre Dame Victory March</i>. <a href="/wiki/George_Gipp" title="George Gipp">George Gipp</a> was played by <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>, whose nickname &quot;The Gipper&quot; was derived from this role. This scene was parodied in the movie <a href="/wiki/Airplane!" title="Airplane!">Airplane!</a> with the same background music, only this time honoring George Zipp, one of Ted Striker's former comrades. The song also was prominent in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Rudy_(film)" title="Rudy (film)">Rudy</a></i>, with <a href="/wiki/Sean_Astin" title="Sean Astin">Sean Astin</a> as <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ruettiger" title="Daniel Ruettiger" class="mw-redirect">Daniel &quot;Rudy&quot; Ruettiger</a>, who harbored dreams of playing football at the University of Notre Dame despite significant obstacles.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Condoleezza_Rice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Condoleezza_Rice.jpg/165px-Condoleezza_Rice.jpg" width="165" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Condoleezza_Rice.jpg/248px-Condoleezza_Rice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Condoleezza_Rice.jpg/330px-Condoleezza_Rice.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Condoleezza_Rice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Condoleezza Rice '75 MA
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Notre_Dame_alumni" title="List of University of Notre Dame alumni">List of University of Notre Dame alumni</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Notre_Dame_athletes" title="List of University of Notre Dame athletes">List of University of Notre Dame athletes</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Notre Dame alumni number near 120,000,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> and are members of 275 alumni clubs around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> Many alumni give yearly monetary support to the university, with a school-record 53.2% giving some donation in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> Many buildings on campus are named for those whose donations allowed their building, including residence halls,<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> classroom buildings,<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> and the performing arts center.<sup id="cite_ref-DPAC_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DPAC-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notre Dame alumni work in various fields. Alumni working in political fields include <a href="/wiki/Governor_(United_States)" title="Governor (United States)">state governors</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> and former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">United States Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> A notable alumnus of the College of Science is Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Eric_F._Wieschaus" title="Eric F. Wieschaus">Eric F. Wieschaus</a>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A number of university heads are alumni, including Notre Dame's current president, Rev. John Jenkins.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, many alumni are in the media, including talk show hosts <a href="/wiki/Regis_Philbin" title="Regis Philbin">Regis Philbin</a><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Donahue" title="Phil Donahue">Phil Donahue</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> and television and radio personalities such as <a href="/wiki/Mike_Golic" title="Mike Golic">Mike Golic</a><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Storm" title="Hannah Storm">Hannah Storm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> With the university having high profile sports teams itself, a number of alumni went on to become involved in athletics outside the university, including professional baseball, basketball, football, and ice hockey players, such as <a href="/wiki/Joe_Theisman" title="Joe Theisman" class="mw-redirect">Joe Theisman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Montana" title="Joe Montana">Joe Montana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tim_Brown_(American_football)" title="Tim Brown (American football)">Tim Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ross_Browner" title="Ross Browner">Ross Browner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Ismail" title="Rocket Ismail" class="mw-redirect">Rocket Ismail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Megan_Duffy" title="Megan Duffy">Megan Duffy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Samardzija" title="Jeff Samardzija">Jeff Samardzija</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Bettis" title="Jerome Bettis">Jerome Bettis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brett_Lebda" title="Brett Lebda">Brett Lebda</a> Olympic gold medalist <a href="/wiki/Mariel_Zagunis" title="Mariel Zagunis">Mariel Zagunis</a>, professional boxer <a href="/wiki/Mike_Lee_(boxer)" title="Mike Lee (boxer)">Mike Lee</a>, former football coaches such as <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Weis" title="Charlie Weis">Charlie Weis</a><sup id="cite_ref-Weis_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weis-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Knute_Rockne" title="Knute Rockne">Knute Rockne</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Basketball Hall of Famers</a> <a href="/wiki/Austin_Carr" title="Austin Carr">Austin Carr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Dantley" title="Adrian Dantley">Adrian Dantley</a>. Other notable alumni include prominent businessman <a href="/wiki/Edward_J._DeBartolo,_Jr." title="Edward J. DeBartolo, Jr.">Edward J. DeBartolo, Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronaut</a> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Wetherbee" title="Jim Wetherbee">Jim Wetherbee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
