Kimmel; Amy Aronson (2004). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=jWj5OBvTh1IC&amp;pg=PA558&amp;dq=muscular+christianity+protestantism+catholicism&amp;hl=en&amp;ei=d0Q3TvKUGonj0QGni520Aw&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=2&amp;ved=0CC4Q6AEwAQ#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>Men and Masculinities: a Social, Cultural, and Historical Encyclop&aelig;dia, Volume 1</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/ABC-CLIO" title="ABC-CLIO">ABC-CLIO</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved August 1, 2011</span>. &quot;As neo-orthodoxy arose in the mainline Protestant churches, Muscular Christianity declined there. It did not, however, disappear from American landscape, because it found some new sponsors. In the early 2000s (decade) these include the Catholic Church and various rightward-leaning Protestant groups. The Catholic Church promotes Muscular Christianity in the athletic programs of schools such as Notre Dame, as do evangelical Protestant groups such as <a href="/wiki/Promise_Keepers" title="Promise Keepers">Promise Keepers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletes_in_Action" title="Athletes in Action">Athletes in Action</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_Christian_Athletes" title="Fellowship of Christian Athletes">Fellowship of Christian Athletes</a>.&quot;</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Notre+Dame&amp;rft.aulast=Michael+S.+Kimmel%3B+Amy+Aronson&amp;rft.au=Michael+S.+Kimmel%3B+Amy+Aronson&amp;rft.btitle=Men+and+Masculinities%3A+a+Social%2C+Cultural%2C+and+Historical+Encyclop%C3%A6dia%2C+Volume+1&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DjWj5OBvTh1IC%26pg%3DPA558%26dq%3Dmuscular%2Bchristianity%2Bprotestantism%2Bcatholicism%26hl%3Den%26ei%3Dd0Q3TvKUGonj0QGni520Aw%26sa%3DX%26oi%3Dbook_result%26ct%3Dresult%26resnum%3D2%26ved%3D0CC4Q6AEwAQ%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rft.pub=ABC-CLIO&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Notre_Dame&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Burns, Robert E. <i>Being Catholic, Being American: The Notre Dame Story, 1934–1952, Vol. 2.</i> (2000). 632pp. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.amazon.com/dp/0268021635">excerpt and text search</a></li> 
      <li>Corson, Dorothy V. <i>A Cave of Candles: The Spirit, History, Legends and Lore of Notre Dame and Saint Mary's</i> (2006), 222pp.</li> 
      <li>Hesburgh, Theodore M. <i>God, Country, Notre Dame: The Autobiography of Theodore M. Hesburgh</i> (2000)</li> 
      <li>McAvoy, Thomas T. &quot;Notre Dame, 1919–1922: The Burns Revolution.&quot; <i>Review of Politics</i> 1963 25(4): 431–450. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jstor.org/stable/1405842">in JSTOR</a></li> 
      <li>McAvoy, Thomas T. <i>Father O'Hara of Notre Dame</i> (1967)</li> 
      <li>Massa, Mark S. <i>Catholics and American Culture: Fulton Sheen, Dorothy Day, and the Notre Dame Football Team.</i> (1999). 278 pp.</li> 
      <li>O'Brien, Michael. <i>Hesburgh: A Biography.</i> (1998). 354 pp.</li> 
      <li>O'Connell, Marvin R. <i>Edward Sorin.</i> (2001). 792 pp.</li> 
      <li>Rice, Charles E., Ralph McInerny, and Alfred J. Freddoso. <i>What Happened to Notre Dame?</i> (2009) laments the weakening of Catholicism at ND</li> 
      <li>Robinson, Ray. <i>Rockne of Notre Dame: The Making of a Football Legend.</i> (1999). 290 pp.</li> 
      <li>Sperber, Murray. <i>Shake Down the Thunder: The Creation of Notre Dame Football.</i> (1993) 634 pp.</li> 
      <li>Yaeger, Don and Looney, Douglas S. <i>Under the Tarnished Dome: How Notre Dame Betrayed Its Ideals for Football Glory.</i> (1993). 299 pp.</li> 
     </ul>
